This function internally converts the HTTPClientConfig (including its TLSConfig field) to an actual *http.Client with properly configured *tls.Config.\\n- The created client is wrapped with OpenTelemetry instrumentation via otelhttp.NewTransport().\\n\\n**scrape/target.go**:\\n- **Target** (line 47): Represents a single HTTP/HTTPS endpoint to scrape. The client is then wrapped with optional RoundTrippers for SigV4, Azure AD, Google IAM, and OpenTelemetry instrumentation.\\n- **NewReadClient()** (line 151): Creates an HTTP client for remote read using the same pattern, calling `config_util.NewClientFromConfig()` at line 152.\\n\\n**storage/remote/write.go**:\\n- **WriteStorage** (line 59): Manages all remote write connections. It ensures that cert files and key files are properly paired and that files exist when syntax checking is not enabled.\\n\\n### Prometheus-Common Integration\\n\\nAll HTTP client creation goes through **github.com/prometheus/common/config** (aliased as config_util):\\n- **config_util.HTTPClientConfig**: The struct containing TLSConfig along with BasicAuth, OAuth2, ProxyConfig, Headers, etc.\\n- **config_util.TLSConfig**: The struct with fields CAFile, CertFile, KeyFile, ServerName, InsecureSkipVerify, MinVersion, MaxVersion for specifying TLS settings.\\n- **config_util.NewClientFromConfig()**: Converts HTTPClientConfig to *http.Client, internally calling NewTLSConfig() to create the *tls.Config with properly loaded certificates, configured verification, and version constraints.\\n- **config_util.NewTLSConfig()**: Converts TLSConfig struct to *crypto/tls.Config by reading certificate files, setting up CA pools, and applying version constraints.\\n\\n### Data Flow Summary\\n\\n1.
